Robber Gu Xiufeng Sentenced to Five Years 172

The robber Gu Xiufeng, a twenty-year-old from Qingjiang, colluded with his accomplices, including the fugitive Li San, to rob the Songhe Tang leaf material store opened by Ningbo native Mi Ziheng at number 111, Huanghe Road, French Concession, at 6:30 PM on the 15th of this month, stealing dozens of large and small silver dollars. They were pursued by shop assistants as they fled to the intersection of Aolihe Road. Gu was arrested and sent to the Special Second District Court for questioning and detention. All relevant details have been reported in the newspaper. Yesterday morning, Presiding Judge Wang Gang of the Special Second District Court convened a criminal court hearing. The police lawyer, Dang Xizhen, presented the case, prosecuting him for robbery under Article 348 of the Criminal Code. The victim then recounted the robbery. The robber Gu confessed to colluding to commit robbery, not daring to deny it in court. Upon reviewing the evidence, the court announced the verdict, sentencing Gu Xiufeng to five years of imprisonment for carrying a weapon and engaging in gang robbery.

Passenger Falls into River While Trying to Sneak onto Ferry 173

The express ferries of the British-owned Taikoo Dockyard Company, which operate between the new customs wharf and Pudong, usually do not allow people without tickets to board. Yesterday at 11:15 AM, as one of the ferries was leaving the Yongchong wharf in Pudong, a seventeen or eighteen-year-old youth attempted to board. As one foot stepped onto the boat's edge and the other remained on the dock, the waterman asked to see his pass. The youth panicked, lost his balance, and fell into the Huangpu River, drowning. A boatman named Cao Zhangbao reported the incident, and the river police of the customs wharf were notified. Later, Wang Caifang of the Huisen Lumber Company on Wenzhan Shilu reported to the police that the deceased was his wife's younger brother and also an apprentice at the business.

Chinese and Russian Morphine Addicts Arrested 174

The medical department of the French Concession learned that a morphine den was operating at number 32, Baoyu Lane, Caishi Street, injecting morphine for people. Addicts from China and the West flocked to it, and the business was thriving. Yesterday (the 25th) around 6 PM, Chinese and Western detectives from the anti-drug department went to the address and arrested no one in the front hall. The side rooms were also empty. Later, in the back rooms, they discovered people injecting morphine. They immediately arrested two Russians and four Chinese, along with morphine, needles, silver dollars, and copper coins. They were all taken to the police station and detained for further investigation.

Russian Boy Dies in Tragic Fall 175

A ten-year-old Russian boy named Bopaofu Sheringski (transliteration), residing at number 41, company housing, number 18, Hualong Road, French Concession, was playing alone on the fourth-floor staircase of his residence around 3 PM on the 24th. He accidentally lost his footing and fell through the central opening of the staircase to the cement floor below, causing a head injury. He immediately lost consciousness. His mother, Fositeli Gaofa (transliteration, twenty-seven years old), upon learning of this, immediately sent him to Guangci Hospital by car. However, due to the severity of his injuries, he died before receiving treatment. The French Concession police were immediately notified, and they sent detectives to investigate. They transferred the body to the autopsy room attached to the Shanghai Municipal Council Hospital on Delastour Road. Yesterday morning, a prosecutor from the Special Second District Court was commissioned, along with a coroner and clerk, to examine the body. They confirmed that the deceased had died from a head injury caused by the fall. After questioning the deceased's mother, the official ordered the body to be handed over to the family for burial.

Xujiahui Observatory: Yesterday afternoon, the weather forecast at 4:30 PM said that Shandong and its surroundings were sunny and cold, with a strong northwest wind. Chronicles

Little Western Paradise 189

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 3: Unresolved Enigma. Peeking Through the Door. A Poor Girl. Quietly Ask. Cherishing Jade Visits a Young Man.

Zhiqian felt even more that Yuanhua was hard to talk to. In front of so many workers, it was really inconvenient to prolong Yuanhua's stay? If he turned around and avoided him, he was afraid that he would follow, which would be even more difficult to explain. So, he walked forward and said, "What do you want from us?" As he spoke, he walked out of the back door of Little Western Paradise. This was a very long yellow earth lane. The houses on both sides were all yellow earth walls. The yellow earth on the ground was like ash in a furnace, very lightly laid. Looking from this end of the alley to the other end, there were only yellow colors, and no one was seen walking. Among them, a family with a low door had a few pieces of zucchini leaves showing on the wall. That little bit of greenness further highlighted the indifference of this alley. He couldn't help but exclaimed, "It's very desolate." Auntie Hu didn't quite understand this sentence. However, she certainly understood the word "desolate". She thought he was talking about the food problem. Looking at Zhiqian's face, he looked very sighing, which she could see a little. She then said, "Master, we don't have anything good to eat, just Guokui fried noodles." Zhiqian smiled, and couldn't find anything else to say for a while. He then looked at the door opposite him. There was a small courtyard inside the door, piled with broken pieces of wood and rotten paper. There were also a few chickens, with droppings scattered all over the ground. Under a row of low houses, there were two yellow earth stoves. The yellow earth wall was blackened for most of the side. The house had a wooden door, which was still tied with many latches. The house was dark, and nothing could be seen. Auntie Hu said, "Master, this is our home." Cheng Zhiqian said, "Does only your family live here?" Auntie Hu smiled and said, "My family can't afford to live here. There are three or four families inside." Zhiqian said, "Three or four families live in this little place." (49)

Remembering Cai Yemin 190

— Zheng Yimei

The other day, I happened to see a newspaper carrying the news of Mr. Cai Yemin's death. The passing of talented writers and the death of celebrities are very regrettable and lamentable. Mr. Cai was from Wujiang. Friends from Wujiang once told me two anecdotes about Mr. Cai. Now I will record them to commemorate him.

Mr. Cai's family had a maid who was intelligent and good at understanding people's intentions. She added incense while he read at night, and her red sleeves were diligent and attentive, enough to comfort the amorous scholar. Mr. Cai really liked her. However, the maid soon sold her smiles and became a prostitute, and quickly became known as Xiao Lingbo. She was very famous. It is said that the long waistcoat that was popular among women at the time was her invention.

The portrait of Mrs. Xu Dai Zhao Da Yuan's wife, Wu Shanshan, was engraved on a monument and erected on the Pingbo Terrace of Yingdu Lake. Later, this monument was somehow moved to a tofu shop in Lili. When Mr. Cai saw it, he spent money to redeem it. Chen Qubing, the deceased revolutionary poet, knew about this and praised it very much. He wrote a redemption inscription, which was widely circulated in literary circles.

Mr. Cai was listed as a member of the Nanshe Society and was very knowledgeable in poetry. He wrote a preface for Gao Dunjian's 30-year Poetry Collection for Bianya Tower, in which he expressed his opinion: "Poetry is the expression of the heart and also a purposeful expression. One person has one person's poetry, one time has one time's poetry, and one place has one place's poetry. Only with the expression of true emotions can there be proof of true facts." This shows a glimpse of his poetics. His poems that have been circulated outside include Zhan Yuan: "The state of the world cannot be discussed. It is sad to revisit the beautiful place and mourn at Baimen. The gardens of one generation have returned to the dreams of deer, and the customs of a hundred years have been paid to the soul of the cuckoo. Where is the vicissitude of the old home? The past is boundless with smoky trees. After all, the imperial spirit of Nanjing is exhausted. How many cold temperatures have there been in prosperity and decline?" From reading the poetry collection of Liu Guzha, Biaoyu Zhai, and the poetry record of Taolu Shigu Zhai, I got a jueju: "The Hedong Poetry Clan was prosperous in those years, and the old general opened the mountain with strict discipline. The rising Taolu occupies a period of time, and the hard words fall from the pen." The title of the autumn flower thief's picture: "Where is the strong wing of the cloud? Thousands of miles of wind and smoke reflect the sunset. I am tired of hiding my wings on the branches. Let me stay with the yellow flowers for the rest of my life." Perhaps there are poems, but unfortunately I have not seen them.

Tidbits 191

— (Baling)

I have seen many friends write letters. If the letter is sent to a certain place in the British Concession, they always write the words "British Concession". If it is sent to the French Concession, they always write the words "French Concession". Friends, are you willing to give away the territory unconditionally? If you are not willing, then I implore you, please do not omit the word "Concession" in your letters in the future for the sake of simplicity.

The Vat 192

— Shijiu

The vat is a necessity for households in the mainland. Without it, water cannot be stored, and water is so important and precious. Especially "rainwater," which can be stored for unexpected needs. Therefore, the vat has become a household treasure. Not only that, but the wealth of a family can also be estimated from the vat. In large households: three-bay halls, four-entrance houses: in the courtyard of each hall, which family does not have a vat? And which family only has one vat? The vats must be lined up on both sides, like servants welcoming guests. Some vats even have tin hats. Some vats also contain goldfish, swimming leisurely and contentedly.

Since the vat is so important, when families in the mainland arrange marriages, some places first ask the matchmaker how many vats the other family has. This custom exists in Dongguang County, Jiangsu. When arranging a marriage, according to the custom of matching families, the matchmaker naturally asks about the family background first, then about the appearance of the son or daughter, and then mentions the family's property, etc. However, this is not the case for families in Dongguang County. The other family's property does not need to be asked, and even does not need to be asked: because as long as you ask how many water vats the other family has, you can determine the other family's economic situation. If there are many vats, then the family must be wealthy; otherwise, the family must be ordinary. The so-called "matching families" is entirely determined by the vat. Even experienced matchmakers often do not wait for the other party to ask about the vat first, but first ask the family entrusted with the marriage how many vats they have.

Look at the vat, it is just a container for storing water, and it is so bulky; unexpectedly, it can be used as a standard for estimating people's property, and it also has such a large relationship with the union of husband and wife.

Two Bad Habits of Citizens—Late to Bed and Late to Rise—

Royal Fragrance Drifting Records 193

— Original by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, Translated by Qin Shouou

Because, according to what I said, when Qianlong returned to Fengtian, he saw that most of the buildings here were very old and the styles were not good. He was a very shrewd and capable person, and he did whatever he wanted. So, he took out a sum of money and had people build many new buildings in Fengtian. This building was naturally also managed by him.

We passed under this city gate. Most ordinary Chinese gates have two parallel doors on the left and right, but they are actually divided into two from one. However, the city gates here are actually two doors, because they are both very large, enough to cover the doorway alone. However, at first, perhaps for special security reasons, two city gates were set up in layers. After passing through these two doors, it was the Forbidden City of Fengtian. A very wide imperial road led directly into the deep palace. When our team stepped onto the imperial road, it added a new color, because the imperial road was covered with golden yellow sand, which set off the red and green figures moving on it. It can be said to be colorful.

There are also some active scenes on both sides of this imperial road that must be described. Because the large team of imperial guards who came with the Empress Dowager had not yet had time to be transferred in, Huaitabu specially selected hundreds of Manchu soldiers from his camp to serve as the Empress Dowager's guard. At this time, they knelt on both sides of the imperial road from a distance. They were about three or four miles away from us. In this gap, there was another group of people. This group of people was also officials from Fengtian, but some of them were not qualified to go to the station to meet the Empress Dowager because their official rank was too low. (159)

Pickled Vegetable Doctor 194

— Meixue

Listening to a Doctor's lecture in college is, of course, commonplace and not surprising at all. Since I became a freshman, there have been visiting Doctors lecturing at our school every week. Last week, we invited Doctor X. Before he came to school, someone in the third grade said, "Tomorrow, the Pickled Vegetable Doctor will be lecturing again. My mouth has been bland these days. It wouldn't hurt to eat some pickled vegetables."

Most freshmen are ignoramuses, thinking: "The Pickled Vegetable Doctor must have made some major invention in pickled vegetables, so he got this valuable degree." Some also doubted, thinking, "What major invention could there be in pickled vegetables? I guess this Doctor comes from a poor family and has eaten pickled vegetables for many years, so he has this nickname." They discussed endlessly, so they asked the senior classmates, "What is the exact meaning of the words 'Pickled Vegetable'?" The classmates said, "Tomorrow is almost here. Listen to a few sentences, and you can understand that he is a Pickled Vegetable Doctor."

On this day, Doctor X came to the school to give a lecture. He spoke Mandarin, and after saying a few sentences, he gave us several pickled vegetables. He said... "Last year, my brother came to your school to give a lecture. Now, I am here again, but now there is the current environment, now there are the current feelings, now what my brother is talking about..." He said six "nows" in one breath. When he said "now," it was as if he were saying "pickled vegetable." After a few opening remarks, he had given us six pickled vegetables. When I heard this, I almost laughed out loud, but I finally didn't laugh. This was because I used a ruse and pinched my thigh hard with my fingers.

Places Visited

A Record of Scenic Wonders of Jiujiang 195

— Wan Gong

Jiujiang is another name for Wuhu, located in the middle reaches of the Yangtze River; therefore, it is also known as Zhongjiang (Middle River). In the past, it was a famous scenic area, then it became a commercial port. Merchants gathered, turning it into a market, which caused the mountains to be covered in dust. Elegant scholars no longer chose to visit and climb! However, the jade-like mountains and charming rivers still possess inherent natural beauty that cannot be concealed! Moreover, today, railway transportation serves as a protective screen for the capital, and municipal construction is progressing rapidly. Exploring the wonders and uncovering hidden beauty, how can one resist? I will now provide a brief overview, serving as a guide for visitors.

Tao Pond | Is the heart of Wuhu's scenery. Zhu Mountain and Fanluo Mountain stand majestically, encircling the streets. A long embankment traverses the area, allowing access for carriages and horses to the city. Numerous winding harbors and gardens dot the pond. Notable ones include: the Li family's Liuchun Garden and Changchun Garden, Liucun Village, Yanyu Mound (Misty Rain Mound), Yitao Pavilion, the Shi family's Youyiyuan Garden (Another Garden), and the Gao family's Shucai Garden (Vegetable Garden). Amidst the misty waves, each occupies a corner of strategic importance. The scenery varies with the weather and the four seasons, especially in spring and summer. In the depths, temporary water pavilions and thatched huts are often erected, connected by long bridges to welcome visitors. Just like a beauty wearing simple clothes and unadorned hair, her natural beauty is all the more evident.

Yanyu Mound | Located south of Tao Pond, it is a peninsula in the pond. Originally owned by the Li family of Hefei, it was developed as a place for leisure during his official duties by Ma Yun, the governor of Anhui. Several exquisite houses were built, where famous figures often gathered to compose poetry. Although more than half has collapsed, the flowers and trees are lush, and the shade of the willows is dense. Leaning on the pavilion and looking into the distance, the beauty of Tao Pond is fully captured.

Zhe Mountain | To the right is the Yangtze River, and to the left is Tao Pond. It is the most prominent of the mountains on the lake! It has now been developed into a public park, accessible by both land and water. Ascending from the southern foot of the mountain, one climbs the steps to a pavilion perched atop. Looking east, the Nanjing-Wuhu Highway winds like a swimming snake. Gazing afar, the outline of Dangtu City is vaguely visible. In the park is the tomb of Mr. Liu Xiping. Mr. Liu, a native of Liu'an, was a pioneer in Anhui's education sector. He was upright and indifferent to fame and wealth. He died at Wuhu Middle School, and his students buried him here.

Fanluo Mountain | Located near Tao Pond, the forests and scenery are equally beautiful as Zhe Mountain. Unfortunately, it is occupied by Westerners, who have built churches and schools on it. Although the red buildings add color to the lake and mountains, it is like a divine mountain on the sea, visible but inaccessible!

Yiji Mountain | Located more than ten miles downstream from Wuhu, it faces the Yangtze River. The steep cliffs are a thousand feet high, and passing ships must pass below. From Wuhu, there is a highway that carriages and horses can use to reach it. It is also occupied by Western missionaries, who have established hospitals and schools. Only with their permission can one enjoy the scenery.

Xiaoji | Is a peninsula on the riverside, located at Erba (Second Dam) across the river from Wuhu. A ferry from Wuhu can reach it in half an hour. There is a Sun Furen (Lady Sun) Temple on it, commonly known as Xiaoji Temple. It enshrines the idol of Sun Furen, the wife of the First Ruler of Shu Han. Common people call the First Ruler a "fierce hero" (枭雄), and I realized that the word "Xiaoji" (蟂磯) is a mistake, and should be 枭姬 (Fierce Lady). According to legend, this is where Sun Furen paid homage to the river. The idol is adorned with jade pendants and pearl rings, truly embodying the image of a female hero. The two serving maids also wear long skirts and carry swords. No wonder a "fierce hero" like the First Ruler would be startled upon seeing this! Beside the deity is a couplet that reads: "Tears of longing for her family fall on the cold Wu River; the soul of Emperor Wang returns to the difficult Shu Road" - alas, I forgot the author's name in a hurry. To the left of the temple is the Huai Army's Zhaozhong Shrine (Shrine for Honoring Loyalty), the ink inscriptions are magnificent, worthy of remembrance.

Pangxieji (Crab Islet) | Located near Lugang, thirty miles upstream from Wuhu. When the river water rises, the large lines resemble fists. From a distance, it looks like a giant crab walking sideways. The shape is magnificent! However, the entire island is made of stone, making it difficult to climb. A small boat can easily approach to within half a mile, but then one must stop rowing and cannot go further. Boatmen who are familiar with the stone paths carry tourists on their backs, wading through the water to climb up. The grotesque rocks on the island are indescribable, towering and steep, as if treading on the edge of a sword. The exquisite and translucent parts seem to be the work of supernatural beings, beyond the ability of the Five Ding Warriors to carve. In the northwest corner, a huge rock can hold a thousand people, standing like a cut cliff. The square shape is as precise as if measured with a carpenter's square. Below, the chaotic rocks and river currents collide, the sound resembling the simultaneous ringing of bells and drums, a truly spectacular sight!

The scenic beauty of Jiujiang is not limited to this. Moreover, I am not skilled in writing, and cannot describe its exquisite and magnificent charm in its entirety. However, I can at least show a glimpse of the leopard's spots! Those who have the leisure and interest, why not come and explore!

Page 13

Free Talk

### Typicality and Reality 196

— Xin Ren

(I)

When we read a work that can be called a work of art, we often find in it the shadows of ourselves or the people around us. Thus, we give the characters in the work emotions such as sympathy and hatred; and everyone has a common feeling: things that they have felt in their daily lives, but have vaguely failed to express, all seem to be revealed in that work.

This is where art becomes art, and it is also the issue of typicality in art that we are going to talk about now. There are two aspects to the reason why artistic works have typicality, and why it is essential.

First, we know that art is different from a camera. No matter how thoroughly and delicately one captures all the events and characters of French society in the first half of the nineteenth century, it cannot compare to Balzac's "Human Comedy." Because the former cannot move us like the latter, and the degree of difference is almost impossible to compare. A photographer or a writer who has not reached the realm of an artist captures a character without leaving a trace, but does not leave us with a deep impression; on the contrary, an artistic painter or writer can make us never forget with just a few strokes or a few words. But the problem lies here. These few strokes or few words of the artist, broadly speaking, are a painting or a work, not something that is casually seen and described; it is a fine wine painstakingly distilled from the raw materials of real life. We can eat as much rice or sorghum (the raw materials for wine) as we want and not get drunk, but if we come across a few cups of real liquor in a hotel, no matter how much you can drink, the end result will be a big or small intoxication. Therefore, art is a comprehensive reflection of reality, a concrete and typical thing.

Secondly, we also know that the most powerful and effective form of propaganda in the world should be art. This is where art differs from slogans, and it is also where art is greater than them. Here, art has a great enlightening and educational power. Art is not a pastime for a few people; it is the most precious spiritual food for the majority of people. Therefore, if art cannot be typicalized, then it is just copying superficial phenomena, just writing about the "foam on the river surface", and cannot express the "torrent at the bottom of the river"; the result is a distortion of reality, or a simplification and mechanization of reality. Such art becomes a poisonous thing, or loses its enlightening and educational power, and at the same time, it also loses its qualifications to become art. (II)

Now, I would like to quote the opinions of several artistic writers we are familiar with on this issue. But I ask the readers to forgive me for saying here first a little bit of feeling that I must say. That is: in the recent past, some people recognized that the previous introductory novels on literary and artistic creation were worthless self-deceiving things (and this is absolutely correct, I think), but those who held this view then put all the artistic confessions of creative experience in the same category, denying them indiscriminately. This is something I cannot agree with. All of human culture is accumulated by generations, bit by bit. Art is not a mysterious thing that is beyond reach, nor is it something that can be created by relying on a little cleverness or "impatience." Therefore, all art apprentices have the necessity to take over the legacy of the past and understand the experience that great artists have exchanged for their hearts. The reason why I quote the following words is based on this meaning.

Let us quote the words of old Balzac. In "The Unknown Masterpiece," he said through the mouth of an old artist: "The subject of art is not to imitate nature, but to express nature. You are not a pitiful imitator, you are a poet! Try to make a plaster cast of your lover's hand and put it in front of you, then you will see the terrible skeleton that is not at all similar; you will go to explore the sculptor and artist who does not rely on accurate imitation, but can convey vivid and lively things. We should grasp the spirit, meaning, and appearance of things and creatures..."

Art is not a rigid imitation, but a lively expression; it is not a collection of trivial things, but a grasp of their spirit, meaning, and appearance. This is typicalization, generalization. Each society has its own special type, and typicalization is complex, concrete, and true, so it is completely unrelated to formulization. Fadeyev has been vigorously advocating typicalization and generalization from the past to the present. Gorky said more concisely: "Artists must have the ability to generalize... Writers who describe a small shopkeeper, official, or worker that they are familiar with, although they can properly make a somewhat successful description of a person, will only lose the social and educational significance. Therefore, it will hardly be able to give us anything in the expansion and deepening of our understanding of human beings and life. However, if the writer can extract the most characteristic class characteristics, habits, tastes, desires, beliefs, grammar, etc. from each, from twenty, fifty, or one hundred small shopkeepers, officials, and workers, and combine them in one small shopkeeper, official, and worker, then the writer who has this technique can create a Type, this is art."

(III)

The above words may have given a glimpse of the issue of typicalization in art. Here, as I am about to conclude, I feel that there are a few key points to say about the following issues.

Also not long ago, some people thought that since art must be subject to the artist's conscious selection and construction, then it is fundamentally impossible to say that art is a faithful reflection of reality. At first glance, this statement seems to make some sense. But in fact, if the speaker does not intend to distort it, it is his negligence.

If the readers understand what I said earlier, they will of course thoroughly understand this issue now. We have said that the superficial description of phenomena, the trivial collection of things, this kind of technique that seems to be "faithful" to reality will eventually turn to the road of distorting reality. Then, the so-called faithful reflection of reality means that the artist should go deep into the essence of phenomena and illuminate the historical necessity in the accidental. In the process of selection and construction, there are two paths for the artist to take: one is to stand on the correct position, follow the above-mentioned road, and deeply express reality in a comprehensive and typical way, promoting history; the other is to stand on an incorrect position and construct things in the work that violate objective laws. But these two roads are chosen by the artist's own worldview, life practice, and other conditions.

Art can only reflect reality concretely and faithfully with the help of generalization and typicalization.

### Old Ancestor Zhao 197

— Li Qiao

People who go to work in the mines for the first time always have to visit Old Ancestor Zhao in Tongjiu...

Old Ancestor Zhao, it is said that he was from Yuanjiang, Yunnan. He had been losing money in Gejiu for twenty years. He became very destitute, and he simply could not maintain his life. He had to think about running away.

He treated the workers very well, and the workers also treated him well. They worked very hard for him every day, but unfortunately, he always lost money every year. This was really something he could not do anything about!

So, one day, he took out all his money. While no one was in the kitchen, he secretly divided a sum of money for travel expenses and a pair of straw sandals on each worker's pillow. Then, he quietly left the mine alone.

He walked despondently on the mountain road. Suddenly, he was blocked by a snake in front, unable to pass.

The snake was long and big, and looked so ferocious! He stood there hesitating for a while, and felt that there was no way to think of a solution, so he had to sit down in the shade of a tree by the roadside and rest.

He was already very tired from walking. Unexpectedly, he fell asleep as soon as he sat down.

After being woken up, he opened his eyes and took a look: it turned out to be two of his workers. They had run from the mine to chase him, because the mine was now striking a rich vein. They cared for the boss and specifically ran to chase him back. As they spoke, they took out the nugget that they were carrying with them and showed it to him, but he still refused to believe it. Moreover, he thought that they were chasing him back to harm him. He refused to go no matter what.

So, there was no way. Later, his two workers saw that he was so stubborn, so they cut two tree branches and tied them into a cradle, and forced him to carry him back.

When they went back and took a look, it was really striking a rich vein!

Old Ancestor Zhao then made a great fortune! At the end of that year, he hired many horses and took all the money he had earned back home.

He had a very snobbish wife. In the past, when he returned home losing money, she looked down on him at all. This year, Old Ancestor Zhao returned home still wearing his old clothes, returning to his home in a very shabby state. (The things carried by the horses were left behind.) His wife saw that he was still coming home as if he was in debt, so she curled her lips unhappily and went to the neighbor's house. Only his daughter brought out a basin of water for him to wash his face.

Just then, the horses he had hired arrived. He felt very sad, he gave a small portion of the money to his daughter, then sadly rode the horse and turned back to Gejiu.

Needless to say, his wife was rushing to chase him with a regretful heart, but he ignored her and left on his own.

When he arrived in Gejiu, Old Ancestor Zhao used all the money to build a temple behind Baohua Mountain.

The temple wasn't far from Gejiu. The road to the mine had to pass through here. The surrounding area was surrounded by many tall and dense green trees. Cicadas and birds were always hiding in the leaves, singing beautiful songs tirelessly.

A small stream flowing out of a desolate and secluded mountain rock and grass surrounded the front of the temple, gurgling and flowing. The water was so clear that it looked like crystal. The sand miners coming down from the mine would definitely scoop up the water and drink it, because people mostly felt hot and thirsty coming from the mine to this place.

In addition to enshrining a ferocious Guan Grandpa in the temple, Old Ancestor Zhao, who was often worshiped downstairs, was also there…

It was just a memorial tablet, but the incense was very prosperous. It is said that people who came here to pray were "always answered"!

Sitting on the stone steps under the shade of a tree outside the temple gate, one could see at a glance: opposite the temple was an extremely lush forest, and below the mountain was a green field. Gejiu was in the distance.

Listening to the pleasant sound of birds, I couldn't help but take a breath gently, and I forgot that I was a "mine worker" who came to visit Old Ancestor Zhao. If I was in the mines, my goodness, how could you have such a leisurely mood to enjoy the scenery!

Note: (1) "Striking the mine" means opening a mine and extracting ore. (2) "Striking a rich vein" means that there are many ore extracted in the mine, which are also good. (3) The ores found after striking a rich vein look like pebbles, called nuggets. (4) A cradle, also called a sedan chair, is used to carry people.

### Sketches on a Train 198

— Xu Xingzhi

Gazing from the train, nature flies past before my eyes, all things flow with the land, and time is the giant wheel of history.

Towering forests stand tall; the earth stretches boundlessly; white clouds in the sky, like giant waves surging.

Cattle and sheep roam the grass, farmers plow the land deeply, the countryside passes away with the setting sun, and the city welcomes the dusk.

Smokestacks spew out black dragons into the sky, factories have become the masters of industry. The train is the medium of transportation, and it kisses the countryside and the city.

### Fifth Lady 199

— TK

### Calligraphy Square (3) 200

— He Wei

Then came a hateful punch on my head, right on the temple or nose. It was not uncommon for me to have nosebleeds from being beaten at that time.

"You think you're a child prodigy, huh, that's just people praising you, you don't know what's good!"

His fist landed continuously on the table, a grunt with each punch, and another grunt after each punch, his nose snorting like a bull. Ink splattered on the calligraphy square, one patch here, one patch there, so blurry that it was impossible to make out. It seemed that I could only end up losing money. My father was especially furious, hitting me and dragging my ear, roaring:

"Don't write for me, you animal! You're putting on airs at such a young age. I'm afraid that even your parents won't be able to ask you to lift a pen in the future, right?"

He absolutely forbade me from writing randomly, but there were also different situations. It didn't matter much if the things brought by poor neighbors were written on. The most important thing was not to ruin the calligraphy squares for the rich! If that happened, my father once threatened to whip me to death, but fortunately I still had a few younger brothers, and bloodlines couldn't be cut off by losing one.

"Write on the paper with better quality first, the rich people deserve to receive profit and auspiciousness, do you understand? " He always instructed me while stroking his beard: "That's right, you must do your best to write, you must write to the point where the brush flies and the ink dances. In order to make the ink color bright and the characters look good, you should add a little alum when grinding the ink!"

Lest I would be irresponsible, he would always stare at me with his eyes wide open, fixedly watching every stroke, every move when I was writing those calligraphy squares for the wealthy families. As if he was especially considerate of me, he would grind the ink for me at those times, press the paper down, and spread the finished writing on the ground. He was also afraid that the materials I wrote on would not match the status of the rich, so he would hurry to turn over the calligraphy squares for me, specifying which ones to write on. If I wrote well, then his joy would be as unpleasant as his rage.

### Ministry of Education Stipulates Textbooks for All Primary and Secondary Schools 201

(Nanjing, 25th Dispatch) The Ministry of Education has instructed all departments and bureaus that the official standards for the curriculum of kindergartens, primary schools, and junior and senior high schools have been promulgated successively, and all publishing houses have been notified to comply with them. The compilation of textbooks for primary and secondary schools based on these official standards is on file. All textbooks for primary and secondary schools edited by various publishing houses in accordance with the temporary standards for primary and secondary school curricula before the promulgation of these official standards, whether they were approved by the former University Council or this Ministry, with the exception of those used in the third year of junior and senior high school, which may continue to be used, all other books shall be invalid from the date of issuance of this order, and schools may not adopt them. As for the textbooks used in a certain subject in various middle schools, before the latest textbooks approved by this Ministry can be purchased from various publishing houses, they are allowed to temporarily self-compile lecture notes as a substitute, but they must comply with the official curriculum standards for each subject and still submit all teaching materials to this Ministry for review at the end of each semester. Order to instruct all primary and secondary schools and publishing houses under their jurisdiction to comply.

Located at the China Vocational Education Society on Hualong Road

From the 29th of this month to the 3rd of next month

Please do not delay yourselves. This announcement."

The Sixth Anniversary Exhibition of the Jing Sheng Biological Investigation Institute Exhibits Specimens and Discovers New Organisms

Sichuan White Bear, Wild Ox, Tibetan Deer, and Swan are Rare in the World, Yu Zhaoqi's Research on Fish in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shandong Shows That Most Have Parasitic Copepods 206

(Special Dispatch from Beiping) The Jing Sheng Biological Investigation Institute held its sixth anniversary meeting on the 20th. No ceremony was held. Ren Hongjun, Ding Wenjiang, Weng Wenhao, Ye Qisun, Yan Jici, Yang Zongpei, Li Shuhua, Xu Songming, Jiang Menglin, Li Zheng, Ms. Pan Cinong, Ms. Wang Wenjin, Ms. Chen Zhonghua, Ms. Shi Xiaohui, Ms. Ma Bo, Ms. Chen Hengzhe, and others, more than 200 people in total, attended. The timber room, animal specimen room, plant specimen room, plant library, fungal and algal specimen exhibition room, fern specimen exhibition room, bird specimen exhibition room, and fish specimen exhibition room each had special staff responsible for reception. The situation in each area is recorded separately as follows:

Six Years of History 207

This institution, jointly established by the Shangzhi Society and the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture to commemorate Mr. Fan Jingsheng, was organized and founded in October of the 17th year of the Republic of China. Mr. Fan Xudong donated Mr. Fan Jingsheng's old residence on Shifuma Street as the site for the Jingsheng Biological Research Institute. A committee was established to oversee all major plans of the institute. It was divided into two departments, zoology and botany, with Dr. Bing Zhi serving as the director and Dr. Hu Xiansu as the head of the botany department and acting director. There were a total of three technicians, two assistants, and one draftsman. The funding can be divided into two categories: foundation and recurrent. The foundation amounted to 150,000 yuan, donated by the Shangzhi Society and managed by the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture for interest generation. The annual recurrent expenses were allocated from the budget of the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture. Subsequently, due to the increasing number of animal and plant specimens and the increase in staff, the existing buildings became insufficient. The China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture decided to construct a three-story steel-concrete building west of the National Peiping Library inside Xisi Arch as the institute's site. It was completed in April of the 20th year of the Republic of China, and the institute moved in for operation. The old site on Shifuma Street was converted into a Popular Science Museum. Mr. Fan Xudong donated funds for repairs, and a memorial room for Mr. Jingsheng was established inside, displaying portraits and commemorative items. The two departments, zoology and botany, prepared specimens, which were displayed in the various rooms in order. Zhang Dongyin, a staff member, was in charge of the museum's affairs. The Popular Science Museum was established on October 1st of that year, and visitors flocked to it. In the spring of the 21st year of the Republic of China, Dr. Hu Xiansu succeeded as the director. In the spring of the 23rd year of the Republic of China, Director Hu Xiansu, together with the Jiangxi Agricultural College and the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture, decided to establish a forest botanical garden at Lushan. The expenses were shared by the two organizations, and a botanical garden committee was established, with technician Qin Renchang as the director of the garden. The founding meeting was held on August 20th. The staff of the institute has increased annually. This year, there are a total of six technicians, six researchers, and fifteen other staff members, totaling twenty-nine people, plus one administrator for the Popular Science Museum and four staff members for the Lushan Botanical Garden. Since its establishment, the institute has spared no effort in researching and collecting animal and plant specimens. Director Hu Xiansu studied the classification of Chinese seed plants and dendrology. Dr. Bing Zhi studied Chinese mollusks and biology. Technician Shou Zhenhuang studied birds, mammals, and fish. Technician Zhang Chunlin studied fish, amphibians, and reptiles. Technician Yu Zhaoqi studied crustaceans and arachnids. Technician Qin Renchang studied fungal plants. The institute also established a wood research laboratory, with researcher Tang Yao specializing in the study of Chinese timber. There are many other researchers, but due to space limitations, they cannot all be listed. The institute has collected specimens in Jilin, Sichuan, and Yunnan on a large scale, obtaining a large number of valuable items. Recently, animal collection has been carried out on Hainan Island, which is not yet completed. Animal and plant collections have been carried out in North China and Hebei. The institute's publications include annual reports, the Icones Plantarum Sinicarum, the Iconographia Filicum Sinicarum, monographs on the Fauna Sinica, and popular science books in Chinese, such as "Common Fish of Hebei" and "Trees Seen in Hebei Province." Each year, the institute exchanges publications with over three hundred foreign institutions. Most of the institute's books are purchased by the National Peiping Library. The library's biological books, especially those on classification, are all housed in the institute, divided into zoology and botany libraries, for the reference of scholars from the institute and elsewhere.

Exhibition Situation 208

The institute's exhibition specimens are in the main building. (1) Room 104, a large room, is the animal specimen room, displaying polar bears, wild cattle, swans, Tibetan deer, black bears, and fish parasites. Room 109, a large room, displays herbarium specimens, including pine and cypress, new type specimens, publications of the institute's botany department, and botanical books. (2) Downstairs, the wood specimen room displays timber from thirteen provinces, including Jilin, Hebei, Henan, Shandong, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Sichuan, Kangding, Guizhou, Fujian, and Guangdong. These were all collected by the institute's researchers and assistants, totaling 3,000 accurately identified timber specimens, belonging to 700 genera, including 1,826 specimens of native timber, belonging to over 270 species, and 891 specimens of foreign timber, belonging to over 400 genera, collected from Japan, Taiwan, Sumatra, the Philippines, India, Germany, England, the United States, Canada, South America, Australia, and Africa. (3) Upstairs, the fungal and algal specimen display room is hosted by Li Liangqing and Zhou Zonghuang, displaying freshwater algae collected from nine provinces, including Peiping, Hebei, Shandong, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Fujian, Guangdong, Guizhou, and Hubei, totaling over 1,000 specimens. The algal specimen room is hosted by Wang Fazan. The bird specimen room is hosted by Shou Zhenhuang. The fish specimen room is hosted by Zhang Chunlin. Each room's specimen trees are numbered, totaling 12,000 animal specimens, over 60,000 herbarium specimens, 3,000 timber specimens, over 1,000 fungal and algal specimens, and over 2,000 bryophyte specimens, totaling over 186,000 specimens. Guests visiting are served tea and snacks in the reception room on the second floor.

New Discoveries 209

The institute has collected over ten thousand specimens in various places, and there have been many new discoveries. The most important ones are briefly described below: (1) The polar bear belongs to the bear family, also known as the brown bear. Its appearance is like a bear, white and coarse. It is produced in the high mountains of Sichuan and is a rare animal. It lives in bamboo forests, often eating bamboo shoots and tender branches. (2) The wild cattle belong to the order Artiodactyla and the family Bovidae. They inhabit high mountain forests, are fierce, and like to live in groups. The meat is edible, and the skin can be used to make leather. They are produced in the high mountains of Sichuan and always descend the mountains in winter to avoid the severe cold. (3) The swan, also known as the wild goose, is similar to a goose but larger, with pure white feathers and strong wings, capable of high flight. It is commonly said, "There is a swan above and a seagull below," meaning it is large and not easy to obtain. (4) The Tibetan deer, also known as the black deer, belongs to the deer family and is produced in the high mountains of Tibet and Sichuan. The males have two long teeth on the upper jaw that protrude from the mouth, while the females do not. The skin is edible and tastes quite fresh and delicious. (5) Fish body parasites. (6) Over two hundred new species of herbarium specimens.

Shou Zhenhuang Speaks 210

According to animal expert Shou Zhenhuang speaking to a reporter, there are over 10,000 fish specimens, mostly produced in Peiping and Hebei. Those produced in Yunnan, Sichuan, Fujian, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang include more than ten rare fish. The Yunnan-produced "Yun Carp" belongs to the bony fish class, with a large head and a pair of small barbels. Similar specimens are also collected for four reasons: (1) Different production areas, (2) Different seasons of production, (3) Different ages, (4) Different sexes. There are many birds in Central and South America that produce different offspring in different seasons because they are in the tropics, so the colors are beautiful.

Yu Zhaoqi Speaks 211

According to fish expert Yu Zhaoqi speaking to a reporter, most fish body parasites are copepods. Ordinary people cannot easily see them and do not pay attention to them. These parasites all live in the gills of fish, like stomach worms in the human body, which are not easy to treat. Although there are many fish produced in China, according to my research results, most of the fish in Shandong, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang have parasites. Currently, over forty new species of parasitic copepods have been discovered. These parasites affect the growth of fish, shorten their lives, and harm female fish in terms of production, but they do not harm juvenile fish. Eating diseased fish does not cause harm because they are cooked, but the diseased fish themselves are harmed.

|| Standard flour for the month of opens on the 26th ||

Flour: Yesterday, after the flour market opened in the morning, the market for each month showed a trend of being strong. The quotation for foreign wheat, Chicago was better by about 1-2 corners, and Canada was better by about 4-8 points. When the opening price was quoted, although this month was close to delivery, the North Road customers were still less active, but the manufacturers were accumulating chips and gradually making up for them. Therefore, the market sentiment gradually became firm, which was better than the closing price of the previous day by nearly one point, and the forward price was better by about one point. Until the afternoon opening, the near months were still recovering due to delivery, the market was stable, and the successive months were soft because the standard gold turned weak. Compared to the morning, it fell by one point. Recently, the exchange rate has been fluctuating, and the future of the flour market has been unexpected. Risks also. As a result, this month rose by two points, November was better by seven and a half, December did not move, January fell by five, and February fell by seven and a half. It was also reported that the exchange announced the standard for March and scheduled to open for bidding on the 26th of this month as usual. At the same time, the supplies for the factory have also returned to normal.

Wheat: Yesterday, after the opening of the futures wheat market, the market for each month showed a near-term strong and far-term flat trend. The standard wheat quotation was better by 1-2 corners in Chicago and 4-8 points in Canada. The recent standard has been stable in the minds of people inside and outside the industry. The current wheat is smooth, and the wheat merchants from various places are not as sad as before. Therefore, on the market side, there are fewer people leaving, and people's hearts are also gradually becoming firm. However, in the afternoon, it was slightly softer due to the standard confusion. The distant period was weak because it was feared that foreign wheat would be cheaper. As a result, this month rose by five points, November was better by six points, December was better by two points, January was better by one point, and February was smaller by one point. The current wheat is being accumulated by various factories, and customers are bidding down the price, so there is no news of delivery.

Overseas Chinese Expelled 256

— Qian

Every day the newspaper publishes news of overseas Chinese being expelled and returning to their country, and photos of many poorly dressed overseas Chinese, and I cannot help but feel indescribable sorrow and disappointment after seeing them.

China has long since become a country with "import surplus," and the amount of money flowing out each year due to the import surplus is difficult to calculate. If calculated according to the outflow of dozens of years, China's finances would have been out of control long ago. Fortunately, there are a large number of overseas Chinese selling intangible goods (services) and bringing back some money; and the success of the revolutionary cause is mostly due to the supply of those poorly dressed overseas Chinese who have been expelled and have nothing to eat after returning home.

Thus, the service of overseas Chinese abroad is the only dumping goods left over from my country's industry and commerce, and the only source of financial supply. Now, because the number of overseas Chinese in China and abroad has increased sharply, they are able to endure hardship and make money, and they are envied by various countries, so they have repeatedly been forcibly confiscated of all their property and expelled; on the one hand, it is hindering the sales of goods, and on the other hand, it is increasing the number of unemployed people in the country. Like now, when China is full of recession, where are there so many places to settle them; and the indirect impact is to cut off some of the sources of wealth brought back, and to promote China's financial crisis.

Therefore, to ensure that my country's financial resources are continuous, in the modern era when industry and commerce and all enterprises are waiting to be cultivated, the only way is to do everything possible to protect the overseas Chinese's activity abroad, so that they can gain some advantages abroad, and then many important national constructions will increase the power of investment, which is such an important and awaiting event!

When Bored 257

— Xu Xizhen

(The sky in late autumn is dyed with severe influenza, and the earth is sprinkled with a gray, plain, and unshaded light. Cars and people are walking on the street, and the hammers in the workshop are ringing regularly: however, this world is dead, plain, lonely, and cruel.

In late autumn, when the wind blows the corners of people's clothes, I think of the red leaves in my garden and the grass chrysanthemums in the corners of the fields.)

Rising up is a smoke-like homesickness.

People who are suppressed by life are like clowns training tigers in a circus. If they let go, they will be swallowed up. In order to live, this world should be completely dynamic: swinging swings, trains on rails, and the shadows of airplanes on the ground.

But on a rest day in late autumn, the mood of "people" is revived || When working, people are machines, without feelings, without sadness, without thinking; but when the mood of "people" is revived, the lines of thought in the heart grow like weeds in April, looking at the cloudless October sky outside the window: gray and white, empty; the heart is like a large piece of cloth that has been bleached, blank, and can be creased.

(Loneliness is like leaves falling on the ground.)

Light a fire, light a strong-smelling cigarette, inhale it, and then exhale it, dissolving the strange and melancholy thoughts into one smoke ring after another, watching them rise and fly away, but in the end, they disappear weakly in mid-air.

I was also surprised that people who are dragged and run by life in the metropolis also have the leisure to observe the posture of the smoke rings? But what can be done? The human heart is an organic combination, different from gears and iron nails. It needs rest and nourishment, just like the human body. Given the opportunity "even for a second", it will not let go and shoot towards thinking for thousands or tens of thousands of miles.

Let memory be the crutch in the hands of a traveler, trying to find something lost on some trampled land in the past; but the result is just as expected, it is a kind of vagueness like the future. This revelation may be of some use to me. It shows that: there is nothing in the past.

And the future, experience tells people, the future is the most unreliable. If there is really a road to the future, then at least as it looks now, isn't it as vast and immeasurable as a cave in a deep mountain? Really, in primitive times, who dared to say that a lonely traveler on a desolate continent could determine whether the plain in front was a desert or a pasture?

In this way, the heart is like flour with water: it is stagnant. There seem to be many hard needles piercing around, and there seem to be soft silks winding around. Struggling and resisting, the result is falling into a viscous blank mud pit, which is strangely uncomfortable.

I remember someone saying: Boredom is a regular customer in leisure. When the door of leisure is opened, it will come to visit.

Suddenly I remembered: This indescribable disturbance in my heart has a specific term: it is boredom!

Terrorist Activity 258

Famine Refugees 259

— Jingyun

"Grandpa, my stomach hurts so much I can’t walk anymore." Da Mao clutched his stomach with both hands, squatting on the dirty ground. Sweat beads, the size of yellow beans, streamed from his forehead down his thin cheeks like a waterfall. His dark pupils kept rolling upwards, and his brows were tightly furrowed.

"Da Mao, just endure it a little longer. While the sun hasn’t risen too high yet in the morning, let’s try to cover a few more miles, or…" Zhang San’s father knew that his grandson had been traveling for days and nights on arid roads, and at the same time, he hadn’t had enough food. His physical and mental strength were exhausted, and his feet felt like they were rooted to the ground, making it truly impossible to move. He thought about the life they used to have at home, compared to the current wandering and drifting, and he felt a pang of bitterness. Tears involuntarily flowed from the corners of his eyes.

Zhang San's father was a simple and honest old man. Usually, when he worked, he wasn't exaggerating or careless, and he had no vices. Except for the occasional pipe or two of dry tobacco during his leisure time; but now, even tobacco was out of the question. Therefore, every year, through hard work, he managed to save a little, and the family's life was quite comfortable. This was something that people in the village envied and considered as a model. However, Zhang San’s father's only son, A Gen, unfortunately died suddenly in the field during the summer three years ago. This made Zhang San’s father believe it was a great misfortune for his family, and at the same time, he resented that he hadn’t accumulated enough good deeds in his life, attributing his son’s death to fate.

Originally, someone like Zhang San’s father, who worked hard, was frugal, and focused on saving, could have勉强勉强 gotten by during this famine year. But, in the first half of the year, his old wife and daughter-in-law both fell seriously ill and died one after the other. At the same time, the price of silk plummeted, causing Zhang San’s father to lose a lot of capital. Zhang San's father had hoped that he might be able to recover some of these lost funds during the autumn harvest. However, since the beginning of summer, the heavens had refused to send rain. The fields were cracked like tortoise shells, and the rice seedlings were all dried up like straw. Under these dire circumstances, the "village tiger" Shen Youcheng, the local constable, led a rain-praying gathering. Under the pretext of setting up altars to pray for rain, and "robbing the Dragon King," he forced Zhang San’s father to hand over money. Zhang San’s father was unwilling to submit to this unreasonable extortion. But how could he possibly stand against the "tiger" Shen, the local constable! At the same time, people who sympathized

Page 19

with Zhang San’s father were afraid of causing trouble, holding onto the principle of "sweeping only the snow in front of their own doors," and didn't dare to offer assistance. Thus, one evening, under the threat of Shen, the local constable, Zhang San’s father handed over the money he had saved.

Now, the countryside had reached the end of its resources. Everything in the house had been eaten or sold, even tree bark and grass roots had been consumed. For the sake of his only concern, his young grandson Da Mao, he finally made the decision to leave his home, which he was unwilling to leave, taking his grandson with him to wander and flee the famine with the people from the same village.

Many famine refugees helped Zhang San’s father, grabbing and twisting Da Mao’s back and tendons. Zhang San’s father’s tears fell like broken strings of pearls, one by one, onto Da Mao’s pale and terrified face.

"Da Mao is probably not going to make it!" Some of the older people watching shook their heads and sighed.

East, West, North, South 260

— Sanduo

I don’t know how to dance, and I’ve never been to a dance hall. No, I've been passively dragged there once. It's said that a "character-splitting booth" was set up that day, but I don't know what it meant. I hope someone who is proficient in dance hall jargon can tell me.

While all industries are experiencing year-round deep discounts and giveaways, it seems that the dance hall business hasn't been affected. The experience of the one night at the "character-splitting booth" made me feel that capitalists who don't invest in dance halls are fools!

However, the majority of patrons in dance halls are university students. Japan has ordered to prohibit university students from dancing. If this has a knock-on effect, then there will be a need for a lot of "buy one get one free" advertisements. So, this investment doesn’t seem very reliable.

A university student I know well said that the Japanese government is too bored, that university students dancing has nothing to do with the government, and that dancing is a legitimate form of entertainment. Does the government expect university students to be buried in the library?

This makes sense, and it's even more impressive. Studying is for the purpose of saving the country, and dancing can also save the country. Since studying and dancing are different paths leading to the same goal, why prohibit it?

Winter Thoughts 261

— Jia Chen

Winter has come, and people who live in the gardens of happiness have changed into the most expensive and latest style of winter clothes. In the glass displays of the big department stores, in response to the seasonal demands, there are piled up many expensive clothes and accessories, waiting for some noble people to consume them. It also brings all kinds of different scenery for these people to enjoy. They have warm houses with hot water radiators, soft and brocaded quilts. Winter is full of warm, dense, and beautiful dreams. When they're bored, they can use a car to send their bodies to the more intoxicating, brightly lit dance halls, hugging fleshy women to pass the long winter nights. Confined within a colorful venue filled with the scent of fragrant powders, with a gold-tipped Chesterfield cigar in their mouth, standing at the window of a tall, foreign-style building, looking down at the street below, at the yellow rickshaw pullers with legs flailing against the biting cold wind, they will sigh through a layer of glass: "How miserable!" But at this moment, their hearts are as soft as wax. Because the metal musical instruments in the back are playing a hypnotic night dream tune again. If it's a late night with swirling snowflakes, swaying on the elastic cushions, and they see homeless children and vagrants in torn shirts standing in the streets outside the car, they will smile with a similar sigh: "How cold it is!" But these people, as if they aren't afraid of the cold, are still wearing those clothes that don't cover their bodies, wandering the streets. What are they doing? Yes, their eyes only see the green lights on the tall, foreign-style buildings, and their ears only hear the decadent jazz music. They see and hear nothing else.

They can't even imagine how some other people spend the freezing days of winter. In some people's hearts and lives, winter is woven into an endless misery, a veil of boundless darkness.

The gift that winter brings to these people is terror, trampling, sickness, and death. Therefore, these people are more afraid of winter than any other season. Thus, they curse winter, they hate winter, they see winter as an enemy. But even though they curse it, winter doesn't stop coming or turn into spring because of it. In fact, spring in winter has long existed, it just grows in another world that has no connection with them. Those other people are singing the praises of winter and admiring winter. Winter also accepts their good intentions, comes to the world with a smiling face, comes to their world. Nature, after all, is duplicitous. It looks down on those who walk with hunched backs and yellow faces. It respects the desires of those who live in the spring of winter.

All the scenery in winter is precious. The emerald-like, shimmering snowflakes fly all over the sky outside the window, plating the earth into a crystal-like silver world. And inside the window with the hot water radiator, in the fragrant house, drinking red grape wine, listening to the crisp singing, and watching the white snow falling outside, you think, how delightful this situation is. Although white hair, in another sense, can become a white knife, under the white snow knife, gasping and groaning. But the white snow does not diminish because of this, it acts as the only embellishment, a beautiful embellishment, for some people as the spring of winter.

Curses, Chapter Three 262

— Xiaolin

Thinking about my own dissolute life, I feel that I am also deserving of curses. I curse myself for knowingly doing things that I shouldn't do, still going to places I shouldn't go, saying that I must change this depraved behavior, but saying doesn't matter, in fact, I still can't change it, and I'm only allowing myself to become more depraved. Isn't this deserving of a curse?

I have long regarded dance halls as demon caves, where many women in gorgeous clothes are blood-sucking ghosts, soulless zombies draped in colorful clothes. But I can think this way, but I can't act this way. From time to time, I still sink into those places that I consider demon caves, willingly letting my blood and energy be swallowed mouthful by mouthful by those ghosts, without cherishing it at all, and without the slightest fear. Because once I slip in, I am no longer myself, but become another person. Then I am completely bewitched, following people into a dream-like, fragrant warmth, forgetting that women can suck blood, forgetting that roses have thorns, and even forgetting myself, forgetting everything. As soon as those rosy lips, smeared with rouge powder, tell a series of sweet lies, I immediately suffer from '烟士披里纯症' [a disease related to being obsessed with romance], even if I understand that the words are lies, I still believe them. So, my past beliefs, my past strong thoughts, are all shattered into pieces by those golden high heels, and my whole body and mind are trampled and panting under those golden high heels. At this time, even if I were to be treated like a mule to be ridden, it would be unavoidable, because my life is no longer my own, but experiencing joy and sorrow because of their joys and sorrows.

At the first light of dawn, I step out of the green glass door, and the cold wind on the street awakens the fogginess in my brain, seeming to clear it up suddenly. I touch my empty pockets. The gold has all slipped into the women's hands during last night's madness. And what have I gained at this moment? Besides an unbearable fatigue and a heart full of desolation. For a moment, I don't know whether to cry or laugh. But at this moment of sobriety, life has once again been filled with stains.

Who can I curse besides myself? That place is fundamentally a combination of hypocrisy and deception. Women are selling smiles and selling joy, so you can't expect them to wear a sad, crying face. It's for life! Who doesn't know that all the joys are temporary, and that time is piled on top of money? And my own money comes from my own hard work, and I lightly send the

Page 20

crystallization of this hard work into the women's smiling faces, into their hands. But no one is forcing me to do this, it's all my own worthlessness. I can think but I can't act. Who can I blame? I should just curse myself. There are naturally many people in the world who deserve to be cursed. But I am the one who most deserves to be cursed.

Rebirth 263

— Ms. Jiong

Time passes quietly, like flowing water! Having left all the old land and old friends, alone in this desert-like environment, spinning and circling. Silent, my soul seems to be floating, without anything to attach to. On this unfamiliar road, I sit alone in a small room every day, not even knowing what I am doing. Borrowing a window on the sun-drying platform to breathe, suppressing all desires, sighing, is this the price we deserve for living? In such an environment, I often feel like this.

In the early morning, the red sun hangs high in the sky, the southern sea, under the bright sun, shines beautifully.

Alone, I stood on the fourth-floor sun-drying platform of the school, gazing longingly into the sky, gazing at my hometown, which is over there? Ah, that golden childhood paradise! How many past years of laughter, past ambitions, past illusions, past school life, past lively friends, it is truly unbearable to look back on. When I think back, waves of old hatreds and new sorrows come over me, like the morning mist covering the distant mountains, wrapping around my heart!

Constant thoughts are locked tightly in my heart.

Living in a foreign land is just like sailing a small boat in the vast sea. Living and dying are with the passage of time, but there has never been stability! Whipped by the cruel whip of life, just like an old horse pulling a freight cart. In the current global economic turmoil, with wars and man-made disasters everywhere, and cries of hunger and cold filling the entire planet, to change my current painful life, unless the entire world is transformed into a new life, a perfect paradise, then my request for "rebirth" will not be as fleeting as a dream!

The bright sun shines into the house, reflecting light everywhere; the gentle breeze blows in, bringing the scent of autumn chrysanthemums. How much are people suffocating in the darkness looking forward to "rebirth"!

Amateur Mailbox

Another Contribution to "Go to the Northwest" 264

Editor:

A few days ago, your publication published an article by Zhou Shaotang entitled "My Views on Going to the Northwest," proposing to organize a "Northwest Development Research Association." I fully agree. The slogan "Develop the Northwest" has long been loudly proclaimed, but very few people have actually gone to do it, so there is no achievement to speak of. There are many reasons for this continued failure, but the biggest reason is that we young people lack a strong organization. The second question raised by Zhou Weizhi in "Prerequisites for Going to the Northwest": "What happens when you get there?" is something we must pay attention to, because the Northwest is a barren place. If we go there alone, we will be filled with desolation and have nowhere to turn. How can we find a job? But if we have a collective organization, a concrete plan, and implement a collective approach to developing the resources of the Northwest, then we can solve this problem. However, we must consider the current communications and politics in the Northwest, as these are closely related to the development of the Northwest. Therefore, while we promote "Go to the Northwest," we must also support the government, promote the Longhai Railway project, develop transportation in the Northwest, and improve politics in the Northwest.

Furthermore, transportation in the Northwest is extremely inconvenient, and news is very isolated. If we want to go to the Northwest, we absolutely cannot act on a whim and rush there rashly. We must have thorough research and practical investigation beforehand. Therefore, I believe that organizing a Northwest Expedition Team is just as important as the Northwest Development Research Association (it can also be said to be part of the work of the "Northwest Development Research Association"). With thorough research and practical investigation, then the collective development of the Northwest will be more likely to succeed.

Now I want to organize this "Northwest Development Research Association," solicit comrades to join, and set up a meeting place so that it can exist for a long time, so that our comrades can continue to go to the Northwest. Among the young people and students who are shouting about going to the Northwest, students account for the majority. It would be best to establish a Northwest Expedition Team during the winter or summer vacation. After the investigation, some comrades would be responsible for the vanguard, while others would stay behind to deeply study the knowledge needed to develop the Northwest, so that they can communicate with each other, research together, and work together. If we work together, even if the Northwest has all kinds of difficulties, we should be able to solve them. My mailing address is Fudan University, Jiangwan. I hope that young people with aspirations for the Northwest will write to discuss all matters related to organization and implementation, and I hope to organize this group as soon as possible.

It has been rumored for a long time that "Silver Stars and Dancing Stars," edited by film writer Yan Meng, is now ready. The content is very rich, the images of silver stars and dancing stars are exceptionally valuable, and it is printed on high-quality copperplate paper. The cover is designed by a famous artist, and it will be printed by the Minxiang Company and sold by Guangming Bookstore as the general agent.

Storytelling 266

Zhongxi 1040

Yao Xiao'an Pang Xueshi Pearl Pagoda 10:00 AM to 11:00 AM

Opening "Crying Banquet"

Parting and reunion are both sad over a wine glass. A farewell banquet is set up at the long pavilion for Qiu Kui. Because my wife forced me to disobey the order, I have to go to the capital for one time. Looking at the blue clouds in the sky, triggering feelings of separation. Yellow flowers fill the ground, expressing the same sorrow. Enter the Jinma Yutang [a metaphor for being a high-ranking official] as soon as possible. Sooner or later, it is difficult to violate fate. Steadily climb the osmanthus tree in the Moon Palace. Swear to not return if your name is not on the Golden List. Take care on the windy and frosty wilderness inns. And on the often traveled path be careful in life. The right way to face the fact that good things are often destroyed, do not lie in bed with bad luck. If there is news from the horizon, a certain Mud Jin [a type of fine paper] will certainly hold your happy news. The horse slowly walks, the carriage quickly follows. The remnant sunset shadow is urged by a whip. Thousands of words of concern, mixed with the dust blowing to [Zheng] Lu’s face. What bitterness there is in life from separation, send you off a thousand miles apart. May the memories of shared minds follow your dreams.

(Hangyun 1180)

Zhang Mengfei Storytelling 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening (Autumn Chamber Lament)

The sound of the pounding block under the moon, intermittent. Tears wet the fragrant silk as a dream is rudely awakened. The hair on the temples is easily disheveled. Leaning on the railing, I see the moonlight. The autumn light opens my eyes to sights that are all sorrowful. The vast landscape is filled with the autumn wind. I fear seeing the swaying shadow of the fading flowers. I hate hearing the heartbreaking sound of the bells. It’s hard to find an entertaining scene in dreams. Time turns into the new autumn clouds over the river. In the deep chamber, sometimes I lift the curtain and sit. Alone in the embroidery room, I secretly groan. I remember often laughing and talking before the small banquet, in front of flowers. It’s hard to describe the ten thousand kinds of emotions. I remember going to enjoy the lotuses with a paddling sound. Hiding the spring in the lotus picking boat. I remember meeting in the red chamber and talking about innermost feelings. Swearing to the same hundred years of heart. I remember walking together in the snowy mountains. Seeing the plum blossoms on the ridge heralding early spring. I remember playing a storytelling song for you. The sound is like jade and the words like pearls, that you can certainly hear. I remember sitting side-by-side on the grassy ground. I remember going to see the bright moon on the pond under the moon. Now there is separation and the soul often lingers in dreams. At Nanpu, the feelings are deeply melancholy. The west wind enters the courtyard as a familiar face. Wanting to ask someone in Guangling to send it to the east. How many stages have you already passed on the road?

Spoken Drama 267

Central-Western (1040)

Guanyin Society's "Romance of Heroic Sons and Daughters": From 7:15 PM to 8:00 PM, An Xuehai and Young Master An extensively discussed their familial joys. Old Master An, having learned about Thirteenth Sister, gathered from her words "meeting in the clouds" that she was someone of substance!

Another strange event occurred, but this time, it was fortunate. Lord Hetai was demoted and fined tens of thousands of taels of silver. Subsequently, An Xuehai was reinstated, leaving Old Master An somewhat puzzled! Suddenly – an Imperial Envoy arrives! Just who is this Imperial Envoy? Highly intriguing!

Hua Xing (2260)

Guanyin Society's "Raising Havoc in Ningguo Mansion": From 8:15 PM to 9:00 PM, women believe that love is inherently selfish, especially when confronted with a rival for their affections. They will go to any lengths to contend with her!

You Erjie has already been deceived, undeniably. Now, Wang Xifeng is further implementing her schemes, instructing subordinates to spread conspiracies!

Wang'er meets Zhang Hua, the beggar, at the teahouse, instructing him to write a petition accusing Jia Lian, of course! A woman's jealousy surpasses human love - is it worth it?

Eternal Life (1080)

Guanyin Society's "Good Youth": 9:00 PM to 10:00 PM

Qiao Niang, like a shrew, has finally fallen. Sadly, her period of enjoyment is brief, and she ends up as someone else's beast of burden. Fortunately, her mouth is still capable, saving her from wandering the streets. However, Jie Yun is a snobbish villain; how could he tolerate an idle person? Consequently, Qiao Niang constantly senses the danger of such reliance, pitifully transforming her fair and delicate flesh into Jie Yun's outlet for asserting dominance! Alas, what is needed in these times is Brother Kong.

Hua Mei (1060)

Guanyin Society's "The Fate of Tears and Laughter": 10:00 PM to 11:00 PM

Fan Jashu, to avoid public attention, uses the pretext of visiting his uncle in Tianjin. Upon arriving in Tianjin, his two younger sisters tease him, mistaking Shen Fengxi's photo for He Lina! Strangely, why would Shen Fengxi's photo be sent to Tianjin? In fact, this misunderstanding originates with Jashu's cousin's wife, who deliberately sent Fengxi's photo, thinking it was Li Yao, intending to pair them up!
